New Trends in Japanese Rural Economy 75

— Special Dispatch from Japan

Due to the global economic recession, heavy taxes, and the unprecedented natural disasters of last year, Japan's rural economy is in extreme distress. Ordinary farmers are finding it difficult to make a living. According to surveys by the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry and the Ministry of Home Affairs, the number of farm households in need of relief in the drought-stricken areas such as Kyushu, Ehime, and Kagawa is 226,181; in the areas affected by crop failures, such as Kagoshima, Miyagi, and Ishikawa, there are 119,941; and in the sericulture areas, such as Yamanashi, Gunma, Nagano, Saitama, Aichi, Mie, Gifu, Shiga, and Shimane, there are 412,926. In total, there are 759,048 households in need. In view of the seriousness of the situation, the government convened a special temporary meeting last year to discuss relief measures. In the regular Diet session this spring, a huge disaster relief budget was approved. In terms of social measures, efforts have been made in recent years to promote rural self-reliance movements. Although these measures cannot fundamentally relieve the rural areas, the trend in the rural economy has shifted towards self-sufficiency, commercialization, industrialization, rationalization, and communization.

The reason why Japanese farmers have become aware of economic exhaustion in recent years is because they have failed to maintain the principle of self-sufficiency and are being exploited by merchants and industrialists. Now, the rural areas are focusing on restoring a self-sufficient lifestyle, promoting self-sufficient handicrafts. In terms of clothing, everyone is using silk and cotton fabrics produced in the rural areas. In terms of food, everyone is using food produced within the village. Even things like wine and soy sauce are brewed by the farmers themselves, no longer relying on the supply of merchants. Regarding fertilizers, which are most relevant to the rural economy, under the leadership of the intellectual class in the rural areas, farmers are manufacturing and supplying them themselves. Just taking this one item as an example, in Gifu Prefecture alone, 3 million yen can be saved annually, because farmers have always purchased fertilizers on credit during the busy farming season, requiring heavy interest payments and passing through two or three commercial institutions. By the time it reaches the farmers, the price is already much higher. However, under the principle of self-sufficiency, there are also some contradictory phenomena, such as rural elementary school students abandoning wooden clogs and switching to rubber shoes. Rural consumers are considering ways to prevent industrialists and merchants from profiting from this situation.

According to the village affairs report of Aobe Village in Shizuoka Prefecture, from the Showa 2nd year to the 5th year, the entire village had to bear a debt of over 40,000 yen each year. Since the 6th year, a self-sufficient economic system has been implemented. All consumer goods, except for those that must be purchased outside the village, are supplied by the people within the village themselves. As a result, not only is there no debt, but there is also an average annual surplus of over 27,540 yen. Since then, many rural areas have followed the example of Aobe Village and are trending towards self-sufficiency. However, today's social life is very complex, and absolute self-sufficiency is impossible. Moreover, the surplus products from self-sufficiency must be transported to cities or other villages. Farmers want to eliminate intermediate retailers and wholesalers and sell directly to consumers, which is trending towards commercialization. However, to implement a self-sufficient production system, it is necessary to industrialize the rural areas, especially during the so-called "emergency times" when soldiers are busy preparing for war. To make the war last forever, it is necessary to first enrich rural industry, so the Ministry of the Army's military budget includes an item for "improving rural industry." The industrialization is most obvious in the rural areas of Nara, Osaka, and Kyoto. Threshing machines, rice milling machines, etc., are everywhere. Other side occupations are also being vigorously promoted.

Another notable trend is the rationalization of rural areas. This rationalization can be divided into three types: rationalization of production, rationalization of private life, and rationalization of public life. The rationalization of production is carried out by agricultural associations formulating regeneration plans and providing detailed guidance on the selection of varieties and the application of machinery. The rationalization of private life involves using empty houses as warehouses, promoting frugal weddings, and saving money. The rationalization of public life includes things like the merging of villages, the reorganization of elementary schools, and the promotion of extracurricular activities. Rural areas throughout Japan are implementing these measures. The fishing and farming villages in Hokkaido have been the most effective. Under the support and guidance of administrative personnel, farmers are implementing joint sales, joint purchases, joint transportation, joint silkworm rearing, joint debt repayment, joint operations, and so on. Many cooperatives have abandoned their business nature and become communized for the benefit of the public.

As this new trend in rural economics unfolds, farmers' thinking may also have a tendency to become radical, which is what the Japanese political authorities are most worried about. (June 11th, Tokyo)

The Chinese and German Embassies Decide to Upgrade - The Issue of Relocating the Berlin Embassy 76

Berlin Correspondence: The German Reichstag held a general meeting at 8 PM on May 21st. Hitler read out his thirteen major points of foreign policy, which lasted for about two hours. This speech, which was related to the safety of Europe, had no empty seats inside the venue, and the road outside the venue was also filled with onlookers. Even the entire Germany listened attentively through the radio, which aroused such great interest. The diplomatic corps also participated in its entirety that day. The ambassadors of Britain, the United States, Italy, and Japan, as well as the ministers of other countries, stood up one after another to congratulate Liu Chongjie, the Chinese envoy to Germany, which attracted the attention of the audience. The German government has formally announced that it will upgrade its envoy to China to an ambassador, and the Chinese government has replied agreeing and taking the same steps.

The idea of upgrading the ministers of the major powers stationed in China to ambassadors has been around for a long time. Because the Soviet Union was the first to take the lead, Italy followed suit, and Japan is now following suit. European countries, unwilling to lag behind, have a tendency to make a sharp turn. Germany, however, is following Britain's lead, agreeing to act together. Each has its own wonderful purpose. On the afternoon of May 17th, at 6:30 PM, the German Foreign Minister invited our country's Minister Liu to meet and informed him that the German government intended to upgrade its embassy in China to an embassy, ​​hoping that China would take the same steps and solicit consent for the new ambassador, Dr. Trautmann. The next day, Minister Liu informed the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs, saying that he had received an order from Nanjing that the Chinese government had decided to upgrade the Berlin legation to an embassy at the same time. On May 21st, Minister Liu visited the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs again and notified that the Chinese government had also replied by telegram agreeing to the new ambassador. The mutual respect between China and Germany has been clearly stated. After the announcement of this news, the local newspapers reported it in great detail. Major newspapers that pay attention to diplomacy have also commented on it. Excerpts from the Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung and the Berliner Tageblatt are translated below:

Deutsche Allgemeine Zeitung: The news that the German government has decided to upgrade its envoy to China to an ambassador will be welcomed by the majority of people in Germany. Other major countries will also send ambassadors to China at the same time as Germany. An ambassador is different from a minister and is the representative of the head of state. This common step taken by various countries is a proper expression of recognizing the remarkable achievements of the government of the Republic of China in recent years. In a difficult environment in terms of politics and economics, China has worked hard to build, revive everything, and create the Chinese nation, making remarkable progress.

After years of internal political disputes, China has now largely settled down. General Chiang Kai-shek has been working hard to quell the chaos of bandit suppression for more than a year, and has achieved success in recent months. At the same time, although China has been affected by the Manchurian Incident, the global economic panic, and the rise in silver prices, which have hindered its upward development, it has still been able to achieve such results without the financial assistance of foreign countries. Japan also participated in this move by the great powers. We secretly hope that this move by Japan is not only a superficial kindness, but also a starting point for the two countries to eliminate old grievances, which would be fortunate for the peace of the Far East.

Berliner Tageblatt: Italy, Britain, the United States, and Germany have successively upgraded their ministers stationed in China to ambassadors. Britain, the United States, and Germany all announced their decisions on the same day. Italy took the lead in advocating the above decision. Since the Washington Conference and the Nine-Power Treaty in 1930, the countries have mutually agreed that this matter should be acted upon jointly. Italy's actions in this regard were a step ahead and took the lead.

Italy's pioneering move was because Japan was trying to get closer to China and had already upgraded its minister stationed in Peiping to an ambassador in order to promote a friendly atmosphere, but the increasing consolidation of the political power of the Nanjing government also had a lot to do with it. At the same time, the so-called "One China Issue" - that is, how China's future relations with Europe, the United States, and Japan on the one hand will develop - although there is no sudden change, it has gradually reappeared on the stage of "world politics." Under the leadership of General Chiang Kai-shek, the consolidation of the central government's position, as well as the economic development that will be associated with political centralization, and China's unpredictable position in the world political arena, have to some extent had the same effect on Italy and other countries and have become the cause of the upgrading of ministers. The Soviet Union has had an embassy in Peiping since 1924.

The interests of Germany in China and China in Germany are almost entirely economic and cultural in nature. At present, both sides are working hard to manage and develop in these two aspects.

The mutual upgrading of the legations of China and Germany to embassies is a foregone conclusion and does not need to be discussed. However, we cannot help but say that the Chinese legation in Berlin, purchased 30 years ago, is old, small, and indescribable. Formerly, the area was still a residential area, but now it has gradually become a bustling city. The legation is adjacent to shops, which is extremely noisy, and the surrounding area is full of restaurants and dance halls, which is a particularly bad environment. Therefore, the legation is often cramped and uneasy during social events. It is said that after Minister Liu took office, he requested a better location. Now that the legation has been upgraded to an embassy in order to enhance the system, the relocation of the embassy must be an urgent task along with the upgrade.

Northern Fujian - Flood, Plague, and Pestilence Plague Each Other 78

Fuzhou Correspondence: In early May, Fujian was hit by severe floods. The southwestern districts, Po Wei, and Changting counties, which were most severely flooded, as well as the villages along the Nanjian Mountains, have been completely destroyed, with crops washed away and no food or shelter. The county governments are currently sending personnel to investigate in order to provide relief. The counties of Nanping, Jian'ou, Songxi, and Zhenghe in northern Fujian, upstream of the Min River, have also been experiencing continuous heavy rains, with the river water rising by more than ten feet. The fields and crops along the river have been washed away and numerous houses have collapsed. The county governments have been telegraphing for relief for days. After the flood receded, due to the accumulation of filth and the hot weather, an epidemic broke out, spreading rapidly and causing successive deaths. The provincial government has ordered the Civil Affairs Department's Relief Committee, the New Life Movement Association, and the Doctors' Association to organize a provincial epidemic prevention committee, allocate 5,000 yuan to purchase vaccines and medicines, and send them to various counties to carry out injections and diagnoses. The county New Life Movement Associations have also launched epidemic prevention and hygiene campaigns, urging the people to catch rats and kill flies, and pay attention to clean eating, living, and hygiene in order to eliminate the source of the epidemic. At the same time, it has also ordered the provincial capital's water and land police agencies to establish quarantine teams to inspect ships arriving in the province from upstream at Hongshan Bridge in the West Port and Sanjiadao in the South Port. If there are any patients, they will be sent to isolation hospitals for treatment in order to prevent the epidemic from entering Fuzhou City. The most tragic case is Zhenghe County. After the flood, it was followed by the plague. The people were already in dire straits, but recently, the areas of Shitien, Wanchang, and Huangdun bordering Qingyuan were invaded by the remnant bandits led by Wen Shaoxiang, and the areas of Tungang, Guachang, and Huitien bordering Songxi were also invaded by Huang Ligui's bandits, who looted on a large scale. Liu [unclear] Ding and Zhang [unclear] Ji's troops are currently engaged in joint suppression. In addition, the roadbeds and bridges on the Pucheng to Yanping, Fuzhou to Mawei, Fuzhou to Dehua, Quanzhou to Zhangzhou, and Longyan to Tingzhou highways have also been washed away in many places. The Construction Department ordered the highway engineering office to repair them quickly in order to resume traffic. At the same time, it ordered the water conservancy engineering office to establish four water gauge stations at Yanping City, Youxikou, Shuikouguan, and Minjiangkou along the Min River between Yanping and Fuzhou to predict water levels in order to prevent flooding. However, according to water conservancy experts, although the Min River channel has been dredged below Taijiang in recent years by a special bureau, the water flow has been becoming smoother. However, the reason why flooding is still unavoidable is that the forests in the Min River's upstream watershed have been devastated by the Communist bandits over the years, and almost all have been cut down. As a result, the once lush mountains are now barren. Once heavy rain arrives, there is no obstruction at all, and in an instant, the water flows down in torrents. Although the flow increases, the river width remains the same, and the water level increases sharply, leading to a major disaster. (June 12th)

Shandong's Deceased Coal Miners - The Process of Issuing Pensions - ...Families of Workers Receive With Tears... 79

Jinan Correspondence: The issue of pensions for the families of the deceased workers in the Luda mine disaster, after donations from various parties and investment by the company, a total of more than 290,000 was raised, and was completely distributed at the Luda current factory office on the 13th. The families of each L[unclear] received the money with tears and dispersed. The details of the process are as follows:

After the Aftermath Committee stipulated that the pensions would be issued on the 12th, in order to ensure that this matter ended smoothly and without obstruction, a general committee was held at the Luda Club on the afternoon of the 12th to discuss a detailed plan. Due to the needs of the situation, four divisions were established to facilitate the process: (1) Supervision Division, responsible personnel are County Magistrate Zhang Yunzao and 64th Brigade Commander Ning Chun. (2) Review Division, responsible for reviewing whether the certificates held by the families of the deceased workers are forged, only then can they be effective in receiving the money. Gao Shoushan, Gu Chi, Zhou Yingdu, Japanese Nakamura, and Ma Yingfu were designated as five responsible personnel. (3) Payment Division, responsible personnel are Rong Zhu Zhong, Japanese Oyama, Wang Zhendong, Li Wencheng, and Meng Junsheng. (4) Security Division, established to prevent irregular behavior by family members at the time, or bad elements disturbing order. Deputy Battalion Commander Liu, Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Guojun, Company Commander Zhang (Tianxiang), and Inspector Zhang were responsible. In addition to designating responsible personnel, relevant personnel were verbally invited to assist.

The Aftermath Committee, considering that the deceased family members receiving the pensions might arouse the covetousness of those with ulterior motives and lead to inappropriate thoughts, or even unexpected events affecting public security, has stipulated several measures, ordering them to temporarily store the money. After the meeting, County Magistrate Zhang Yunzao gave a sincere speech to the village chiefs of the related villages at the Luda Company's on-site office, saying that the unprecedented catastrophe that occurred at Luda was not only a misfortune for Luda Company itself, but also a great misfortune for the local people. The aftermath measures have been determined by Chairman Han and Consul General Nishida at the mine to determine the amount of the pension, giving 330 yuan to each person. It has been determined that it will be issued tomorrow. Considering that the family members of the deceased will inevitably arouse the covetousness of villains, leading to theft or robbery, or even endangering their lives, it is of great importance. In order to prevent this from happening, the Aftermath Committee has designated the Third Section of the County Government, the Chamber of Commerce, and the Post Office in the city as places for the family members of the deceased to store the pensions, which can be freely withdrawn afterwards. It is stable and safe, and it is guaranteed to be safe. I hope that you will relay to the family members of the deceased to implement it earnestly. The order of receiving the money for each village was also stipulated. On the 13th, the distribution will first be given to Pingdeng Village (i.e., the South Factory) and Ziyou Village (i.e., the Northeast and Northwest factories), as well as other villages attached to Yi. On the 14th, the distribution will be given to people from other villages who live in Pingdeng and Ziyou villages. On the 15th, the distribution will be given to foreigners who live in Pingdeng and Ziyou villages who have no property here. On the 15th, they are required to leave the country. I hope that you will all be jointly responsible for this incident so that it can be safely completed.

Gu Chi, the Standing Director of the Trade Union, and Wang Guojun, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, were afraid that the village chiefs still did not understand the significance of this, or ignored it and considered it unimportant. Therefore, at 7:00 PM on the 12th, they gathered the village chiefs again to speak at the Trade Union, reiterating the significance of what County Magistrate Zhang said, and stating that if the deceased family members and family members have disputes over the pensions they received, the village chiefs who are more aware of the situation can submit the details, together with their criticism, to the Aftermath Committee for reference, and can also order their family members to fully state their personal reasons in writing and submit them to the Trade Union or the Public Security Bureau to be forwarded to the Aftermath Committee for reference. The meeting adjourned at 8:00 PM.

Since the occurrence of this tragic incident, all parties related to the company and the political authorities have donated money to comfort the survivors. In addition to the donations received and distributed several times in the past few days, the company has recently received donations from the Qingdao General Company's mining office staff, totaling 1,134.88 yuan, which have been scheduled to be distributed together with the pensions on the 13th. It is said that the batch of donations included 1,000 yuan donated by Jin Yunpeng, 900 yuan donated by Japanese Ichikichi, 500 yuan donated by Gao Qingchang, and other Japanese staff members also donated their entire month's salary. However, Song Biru, the Chinese deputy director of the mining office, only donated 30 yuan, which is less than one-tenth of his monthly salary, so it is quite dissatisfied with by the general public.

Anhui Province: Water Conservancy and Highway Construction; 42 Highway Lines Completed, Totaling 4,200 Kilometers 80

Embankment Repairs Totaling 8,000 Kilometers; River Dredging Exceeding 2,000 Kilometers; Wuhu Communication: Anhui Construction Bureau Chief Liu Yiyan. Since the recovery of bandit areas in Jiangxi, various construction projects have advanced rapidly. As a model example, Liu traveled from Anhui to the capital at the beginning of the month, thoroughly inspecting various areas. After completing his business, he detoured to Zhejiang, passing through Hangzhou to reach Beijing.

He presented the past construction status and future plans of Anhui Province to the central government. On the 13th, he arrived in Wuhu from Beijing and met with the Wuhu Engineering Bureau Chief and the police chief, discussing implementation methods for construction in Wuhu. It is planned to first build roads along the docks, with funding either from public bonds or from the finance department, supplemented by local resources. A decision will be made upon his return to the province. Mr. Liu departed at 3 PM that afternoon, taking a fast boat back to Anqing. According to his statements before departure, the status of highway and water conservancy construction in Anhui Province is as follows:

Highways: Since September of the 21st year, Anhui Province has been rapidly constructing highways according to the main and branch lines decided in the Three Provinces and Seven Provinces Highway Conferences, as well as important routes designated by Anhui Province. As of the most recent count this year, 42 lines have been completed and opened to traffic, totaling 4,224 kilometers. Of these, 958 kilometers have paved surfaces and completed formal bridges. According to the routes determined by the Seven Provinces Highway Conference and the important routes designated by Anhui Province, there are over 6,000 kilometers in total. The proportion of currently completed and open lines accounts for 70% of the total. Currently under construction are six lines, including the Sheng-Yin Road (Anqing to Yin Jia Hui in Guichi) and the Shu-Liu Road (Shucheng to Liu'an), totaling 318 kilometers. Eleven routes, including Wu-Wu and Tai-Su, totaling 560 kilometers, have been surveyed or measured and are planned for construction soon. Eight routes, including Wu-Qing-Shou-He, totaling 917 kilometers, are in the planning stage. However, in Anhui Province, which has historically lacked road construction funds and has been plagued by frequent famines, the achievements so far have required tremendous effort. Further progress still relies on the assistance of the National Economic Commission to achieve complete success.

Water Conservancy: Anhui Province borders the Yangtze and Huai Rivers, making water conservancy extremely important. In the past, due to the laziness of the people and the neglect of annual repairs, coupled with the scarcity of public funds, the situation deteriorated daily. It was not until the great flood of the 20th year that people became aware of the need to both educate and supervise, formulating measures for phased advancement, learning from past mistakes, and preventing both floods and droughts. Implementation began in October of the 21st year and the first phase of work was completed in May of the 22nd year. The second phase was completed in September of the same year, and the third phase was completed in June of the 23rd year. The first two phases involved patching and emergency rescue and were not statistically detailed. Only the third phase had estimated and actual records. The work completed in the third phase included: (A) Repairing over 80 kilometers of embankments, adding over 46 million cubic meters of earth; (B) Dredging over 2,000 kilometers of rivers and ditches, removing over 20 million cubic meters of earth; (C) Increasing the volume of water storage ponds by over 3.7 million cubic meters. Starting in October of the 23rd year, the fourth phase of water conservancy projects continued to focus on both drought and flood prevention, with ongoing education and active implementation. Embankments in various areas are being repaired, and waterways are being dredged, including the major tributaries of the Huai River system, such as the West Fei River, Qian River, North Fei River, Yin River, Jie River, South and North Tuo Rivers, Bian River, and Shi Liang River, as well as other smaller rivers. As for the project funding, after much fundraising, only 80,000 yuan in cash and 6,500 shi of relief grain were obtained. These funds are being allocated to dredge the Chao Lake Shi Kou waterway and rivers within the Hua Yang water conservancy area, with construction scheduled for completion during this year's flood season. (14th)

Zhenjiang: Long Drought Finally Ends with Sweet Rain 91

Due to the long drought, farmers and ordinary people alike were hoping for rain. However, every day was a scorching sun and dry wind sweeping the land. Although the mornings and evenings were cooler, the afternoons were unbearably hot. All living things felt parched, and people felt listless. The meteorological observatory forecast that there would be a change in the weather yesterday. Until noon, there were no clouds in the sky, and the heat was even worse. In the afternoon, clouds suddenly appeared, coming slowly from the west. After - o'clock, the clouds gradually thickened, still revealing the eastern corner. At o'clock, the rain started lightly. Those who were happy said that if it could rain for a day or two, how good would that be? But in a moment, the raindrops thinned out. Although the ground outside the West City was moist, it only rained for about ten minutes, and there were only a few drops in the city. On the morning of the 15th, the weather was cloudy and sultry. At 10 o'clock, it rained, although there was no thunder and lightning to add to the atmosphere, the rain was not small, and the amount of rain must be large.

Overseas Chinese Expelled from the Dutch East Indies Return to Guangdong and Fujian Provinces; Refugees Do Not Arrive in Shanghai When Dutch Ship Docks 99

Central News Agency reports that following the expulsion of overseas Chinese from the Dutch East Indies, a significant number of our compatriots were forced to return home. A previous telegram indicated that 216 overseas Chinese from the Dutch East Indies were aboard the Dutch vessel "Tsjisa Dani" bound for Hong Kong and Shanghai. The ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning, and local overseas Chinese affairs agencies dispatched personnel to provide assistance. However, the expected refugees were not on board. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Take Over Inland River Shipping Today; Chen Wei-qing Appointed as Manager; Divided into Four Groups for Takeover of Various Vessels 100

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is scheduled to take over inland river shipping today. Yesterday, the general manager was appointed, and the methods for group takeover were determined. Details are as follows:

**Appointment of Staff**

Among the 25 shipping routes, 13 are leased out, while important trunk lines such as Shanghai-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Lake, Shanghai-Suzhou-Wuxi-Changzhou, etc., are operated by the company itself. Several preparatory meetings have been held to discuss the operational directions for the self-operated routes. Chen Wei-qing, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Company, will concurrently serve as the manager of inland river shipping, and Xin Yao-xiang will be the director of the Zhenjiang Inland River Branch.

**Leased and Taken Over**

Chen, also the General Manager, has decided to take over the shipping routes operated by the company, and will immediately, together with the handover committee member sent by the Zhejiang Construction Department of Hangzhou, take over the ships, goods, and public property of the shipping company and its branches. It is currently planned to establish four groups for takeover. The first group will take over the ships, goods, wharves, and public property of the Shanghai Inland River Bureau first. The second group will take over the Zhenjiang Branch and its ships. The third group will take over the Hangzhou-Lake Branch and its ships. The fourth group will take over the branches, ships, and public property in various locations of Zhenjiang-Huai'an. After the four groups have completed the takeover, procedures for opening business will be carried out.

**Difficulty in Leasing**

Leasing is done through bidding, and the decision is made by the seven-member organizing committee. Several batches of people have bid in recent days, but the offered rents are too low and significantly differ from the company's proposed amounts, so no qualified bidders have been found. The bidders likely believe that since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is unwilling to operate these routes itself, there is no certainty in business, so they are unwilling to offer large rents, fearing future losses.

Delegation of the Association for Assisting Overseas Chinese in Siam Went to the Capital Last Night to Petition the Government to Negotiate 103

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Joint Association of Various Groups in this City for Assisting Overseas Chinese in Siam, after the second standing committee meeting, decided to send Guangdong Fellow Association representative Zheng Ji-jie, Overseas Chinese Joint Association representative Huang Jian-zhong, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce representative Zhang Nan-yin, Chaozhou Fellow Association representative Guo Qi-ming, Ningbo Fellow Association representative Dong Xin-qin, and the Overseas Chinese Joint Association Secretary Chen Cheng-qin to Beijing on the 10 p.m. express train last night to petition the government. They will stay in Beijing for about four or five days and then return to Shanghai to proceed to Hong Kong and Guangdong to carry out the ban on Siamese rice. The petition of the delegation, the official letter to the Siam investigation delegation, and the telegrams from home and abroad are recorded below.

**Petition**

To: The Shanghai various groups assisting Siamese overseas Chinese joint association, for the Siamese government's arbitrary harsh example, oppressing the overseas Chinese, sincerely beg you to conduct serious negotiation, and swiftly establish a trade treaty with the country, in order to prevent the overseas Chinese in Siam from suffering at the hands of another race. We Chinese people do not hesitate to abandon our villages and leave our homes, venturing far across the seas, migrating to Indochina and the South Pacific islands. Since the Tang Dynasty, there have been people doing so, and since the opening of the seas, more and more Chinese people have gone abroad, especially to Siam. Statistics show that there are no less than three million of them. Historically speaking, Siam has long been a bulwark of our country, as close as lips and teeth. Geographically speaking, Siam's mountains and rivers mostly originate in our country, closely linked as one. Furthermore, in terms of race and religion, everything has a close relationship with our country. Not only that, but the contributions of our overseas Chinese to Siam are countless from ancient times to the present. People like Zheng Zhao, who led righteous soldiers to fight the Burmese in bloody battles, saving a country that was about to fall and establishing immortal achievements, and people in various industries such as commerce, industry, agriculture, and forestry, who were planned and operated by overseas Chinese, cutting through thorns and opening up paths, are the reason for today's prosperity. Otherwise, Siam would not have been able to survive like Vietnam, which was lost to France, and would have been destroyed by the British like Myanmar. Siam has been able to stand tall to this day. Even if the Siamese people do not regard our country as their suzerain, they should still treat overseas Chinese preferentially in every generation, remembering the source of their water. If they do not plan this way, they will become arrogant and forget the grace of re-creation and repay kindness with resentment. Harsh examples such as the import tax, residence tax, return tax, and literacy test that restrict overseas Chinese from entering the country were successively promulgated between 1928 and 1933, making it difficult for Chinese people to come to Siam, causing the number of immigrants to decrease sharply. Even for those who have already entered the country, they have implemented a sinicization policy, such as promulgating the Nationality Law, adopting the principle of birthright, recognizing that the children of overseas Chinese born in Siam are all Siamese and should be subject to military service obligations like the Siamese people, but not enjoy the same rights as the Siamese people. They have also cracked down on overseas Chinese education, closed Chinese schools, and recently forced overseas Chinese to specialize in Siamese literature and not be allowed to study Chinese. The schools established by overseas Chinese in Siam have no room to struggle. In other industries such as commerce and industry, there are also no restrictions. The viciousness of their methods is rarely seen in recent times. How can we bear to sit idly by and not save them? People from all walks of life in Shanghai are filled with righteous indignation and vow to back the overseas Chinese in Siam and force the Siamese government to abolish all kinds of harsh examples and improve the treatment of overseas Chinese. In addition to the organization of the joint association of various groups, the situation has been telegraphed to you in the past. Now, we recommend Huang Jian-zhong, representative of the Overseas Chinese United Association, Zhang Nan-yin, representative of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Zheng Ji-jie, representative of the Guangdong Fellow Association in Shanghai, Dong Xin-qin, representative of the Ningbo Fellow Association in Shanghai, and Guo Qi-ming, representative of the Chaozhou Fellow Association in Shanghai, to go to Beijing to petition. We beg you to forward the message to the National Government to send envoys to the Siamese government for serious negotiations and to swiftly establish a trade treaty with that country to protect the rights and interests of the overseas Chinese in Siam. The petition is urgently waiting for orders. The petitioner respectfully presents this petition.

**Letter to the Investigation Delegation**

Respectfully, we recently heard that your delegation has arrived, and our government, representing the people, has welcomed you. Our association, and the various groups affiliated with it, also express their utmost respect. In the midst of this festive atmosphere, our association is reluctant to raise other issues, forcing them upon your delegation, but in recent times, your country's mistreatment of overseas Chinese has intensified, making it unbearable, like a fishbone stuck in our throats that must be spat out. Therefore, on the day of your delegation's arrival in Nanjing, we specifically mention the close relationship between our two countries in the past and the disputes that have arisen now, for your delegation's review. Our country stands tall in East Asia, with a history of 5,000 years. Its past cultural development and the tolerance, endurance, and hard work of its national character have long been praised by the world. Therefore, in the past, when the country was strong, its prestige reached the small countries surrounding it, and they all paid tribute and sent envoys. Your country was also one of the vassal states. Although internal affairs were autonomous, the orders of the Chinese court reached far and wide. The relationship between our two countries can be seen in this. Since the eastward expansion of European powers, which eroded and swallowed up territories, many Asian countries have been destroyed by British, Russian, and French powers or have been reduced to semi-colonies. In this precarious situation, the only countries that have been able to maintain a precarious situation, strive for self-improvement, and still stand tall today are our two countries, as well as Japan, Persia, Afghanistan, Nepal, Turkey, and Arab countries. At a time when nationalism is prevailing in the world, imperialists are doing everything possible to invade, and weak countries are also trying to revive their nations to compete in the world. The situations of our two countries are similar. The Chinese people residing in your country not only sympathize with your country's efforts to strive for self-improvement but also bravely defend your country against foreign aggression, cutting through thorns and opening up paths. The reason for this is that our two countries have blood ties and are as close as brothers and sisters. Therefore, overseas Chinese have made great contributions to your country and are different from other countries' overseas residents. The Siamese should treat overseas Chinese with special preference, rewarding virtue and repaying kindness. How can they repay kindness with resentment? First, they promulgated immigration laws to restrict the entry of overseas Chinese, and then they forced education and closed Chinese schools. These harsh examples are not applied to overseas residents of other countries in Siam but only to overseas Chinese. How can this be considered fair? The intention of your country is nothing more than to assimilate our more than three million overseas Chinese to strengthen itself. It may be advantageous for its own purposes, but if we put ourselves in their shoes and your country's overseas residents are also subjected to heavy oppression by other countries, what would your country's officials and people think? Our association was shocked to hear about your country's destruction of overseas Chinese. At first, we were skeptical, and then we were heartbroken. If people of the same kind kill each other, our country will inevitably suffer losses, and your country may not have much benefit. For the sake of Sino-Siamese friendship and East Asian peace, instead of the snipe and clam fighting, only benefiting the fisherman, why not maintain the spirit of cooperation in the past, have a good beginning and a good ending, and coexist and prosper together? If our humble opinion is adopted, we hope that you will forward it to your government to abolish all kinds of harsh examples and improve the treatment of overseas Chinese as soon as possible, so that the feelings of the people of the two countries will not be broken. We would be very grateful. Respectfully, the Shanghai Various Groups Supporting Siamese Overseas Chinese Joint Association

**Telegram to All Circles**

Recently, a telegram was sent to the Central Party Department and the National Government, stating: "Since the news of the Siamese government's oppression of overseas Chinese has spread like wildfire, the people of the country are filled with righteous indignation. China and Siam are brotherly nations, and both are agricultural countries. Not only are the races and religions similar, but in terms of history and geography, they are as closely linked as the sides of a cart, sharing weal and woe. At a time when the world is turbulent and uneasy, in order to maintain East Asian peace, we weak nations should unite in spirit and help each other in the same boat. However, the Siamese government does not distinguish this and regards our overseas Chinese as easy to bully, promulgating all kinds of harsh examples and destroying them with all their might. Their ambitions are rampant, and they want to assimilate our three million overseas Chinese in Siam before they are satisfied. The severity of the situation is beyond anything else. Overseas Chinese are the mother of the revolution, as stated by the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. Although our country is now unified internally, the communists have not yet been completely wiped out, and unequal treaties have yet to be abolished. In the future, if we want to revitalize the nation, we will need overseas Chinese even more, so we must not ignore them. Moreover, the Siamese case is not a simple problem of the overseas Chinese themselves but is related to the survival of the entire country and nation. The various groups in Shanghai are alarmed by the warning of "treading on frost, hard ice," and dare not remain silent. Therefore, in the last month, they organized the Shanghai Various Groups Association for Assisting Overseas Chinese in Siam. Its only purpose is to promote the Siamese government's reflection and improve the treatment of overseas Chinese. It will not stop until it achieves its goal. In addition to further uniting compatriots at home and abroad to support the overseas Chinese in Siam, we should telegraph to you to quickly determine a policy, first to establish a formal international agreement with the Siamese government. If the authorities still have no sincerity, please consider the ban on Siamese rice imports, taking into account local conditions and consulting on appropriate measures, and implement them as soon as possible. Then the Siamese, who are arrogant and regard our country as a rice market, may eventually have the heart of regretting their mistakes, so that the overseas Chinese in Siam will not be trapped in anarchy and terror for a long time and be slaughtered by them. The future of the country and the people is very fortunate. The telegram is trembling and cannot bear to wait urgently for orders, etc. Before a trade treaty is established between China and Siam and the Siamese government improves the treatment of overseas Chinese, we should have a firm position, orderly steps, and jointly implement effective measures to resist Siamese goods to deal with them, hoping that the oppressed overseas Chinese can be relieved of their suffering. Since this matter is of great importance, it cannot be accomplished without the efforts of everyone. We hope that the party committees and governments of various provinces and cities will be responsible for guiding various groups at home and abroad to jointly support or quickly request the government to negotiate seriously, or awaken compatriots to deal with it in unison. This will not only save overseas Chinese from imminent danger but also benefit the future of the country and the nation. We hereby send this telegram, hoping that you will consider it."

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and Others Presented a Petition Asking Not to Change the Dredging Plan 108

The New News Agency reports that the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association jointly submitted a document to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the National Economic Commission, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the Department of Construction to implement the dredging plan to benefit the commercial port. The original text is as follows:

**Dredging Plan Should Not Be Changed**

The petition is for the water of the Huangpu River, which is related to the national commercial economy. Now that the dredging plan is being implemented in order, it is not appropriate to discuss changes lightly. We humbly submit our views, hoping that you will examine and verify them, in order to attach importance to the commercial port and maintain water conservancy. It has been found that on May 3 of this year, the Shanghai newspapers reported that the Pudong Fellow Association submitted a document to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government, suggesting that the Huangpu waterway is gradually becoming shallow and narrow, which hinders commercial affairs and farmland, and requested the establishment of an organizing body, with four articles attached to the suggestion. According to the original text, the Huangpu River originates from Dianmao, with vast waves, and is the hub of national commerce and the lifeline of farmland in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. According to the old records of Songjiang Prefecture, the river surface is six or seven miles wide, but the report of the Qing Dynasty Dredging Bureau's actual measurement shows that Dongjiadu is 145 English feet wide. The land is close to the commercial port, and the land price is relatively high. People who seek profit fill it in the morning and occupy it in the evening. If it is not restricted, it will become like a ditch, and the fertile land of our Jiangsu and Zhejiang will become stony fields, and large ships will not be able to reach Huzhou and Hangzhou directly, which will make transportation inconvenient and reduce commercial activities, etc. After reading it, how can we not be suspicious? All four articles attached to the suggestion, except for one or two articles that are related to the Huangpu waterway, the other three or four articles belong to the scope of local administration. Although the association's suggestion is purely out of love for the hometown and for the sake of planning ahead and preventing trouble, it does not know that Shanghai is one of the four major commercial ports in the world, and the Huangpu waterway should be fully planned for international trade and ship transportation, considering it as the first commercial port in Southeast China. Although it is possible to take care of farmland in Jiangsu and Zhejiang and navigation in Huzhou and Hangzhou, the relative importance and urgency of the two should be compared. How can they be talked about in the same breath?

**The Dredging Project Has Significant Effects**

The Dredging Bureau was established in the first year of the Republic of China, and its affairs concern the Huangpu waterway and port affairs. Therefore, it first emphasized attracting specialized talents, which has become a past event and is especially obvious to everyone. Even in recent years, the most prominent thing is that since Director Song Ziliang took office, he has actively implemented improvements. The project of the existing waterway has been increasing the depth of the Huangpu River year by year. Giant ships with a draft of 30 English feet can now pass through without hindrance, and the progress of the dredging project has increased from 530,000 cubic feet per year to 1,070,000 cubic feet. The efficiency of the project has made rapid progress, and the accumulated deposits in the Bureau over the years have been transferred from foreign banks to the Central Bank, invisibly recovering great sovereignty. Moreover, the change in water conservancy is a specialized subject. In the distance, the Baihe River in Tianjin passes through Dagu. Although it has been dredged many times, costing no less than tens of millions, it is still suffering from siltation and has not achieved results to this day. The Yellow River has been called a disaster since ancient times, and the strategies for governing the river have been written into special books, filling countless books. The country spends huge sums of money every year, but breaches are still frequently heard. From this, it can be seen that governing rivers is not an easy task. It is important to be able to plan and implement a predetermined plan day by day and month by month in order to achieve success. How can it be changed easily? This is one reason. Moreover, the Dredging Bureau, in view of the increasing siltation of the Suzhou River waterway, which is related to the transportation of rice from the inland to Shanghai, also uses it for the transportation of garbage ships, etc. Once the ships are crowded, it is related to the people's food and hygiene. Song and the former Mayor Zhang, and the relevant agencies, planned to establish a dredging committee for the Wusong River and decided on a six-year plan, which is gradually being implemented this year. Since the 20th year of the Republic of China, the amount of sludge dug out has exceeded 300,000 cubic feet. The obvious effect of this can be seen here.

**No Need to Establish Another Organization**

In addition, the Bureau's construction of a large dredging ship has just been completed. Its efficiency and speed are excellent. Now that the shoal at the mouth of the Yangtze River has always been an obstacle to the navigation of import and export ships, the Bureau has decided to implement a dredging plan and is currently carrying out the work. This matter is of great importance. It is important to plan for the long term and seek a permanent solution for the commercial port. How can it be changed lightly? This is the second reason. Observing the above situation, although the annual fee of the Dredging Bureau is a huge sum of 460,000 taels, it is actually all used for the project. If one were to look at the Bureau's report, it is feared that the amount used is more than this, which is unknown to outsiders. Now, the Bureau is recruiting graduates from universities to train domestic water conservancy talents. Other water conservancy agencies, such as the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission and the Taihu Water Conservancy Commission, often ask for dredging services, which shows the need. It is not appropriate to change the important Dredging Bureau, which has made great achievements, lightly because of the one-sided opinions of individual groups. Even if another organization is established, it may not be better than the current one. This is why the association believes that it is absolutely impossible. After the case was put forward for discussion, everyone agreed and unanimously decided to submit their views in writing, hoping that you will examine and verify them and not be moved by unfounded rumors, so as not to let the Dredging Bureau fail to complete its work, in order to attach importance to the commercial port and maintain water conservancy. The petitioner is eagerly waiting for orders. Respectfully submitted to the National Government Construction Office, the petitioners are Yu Zuoren, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and Yu Hede, Chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association.

National Association of Accountants Presents to the Ministry of Finance to Amend the Supervision and Liquidation Methods 109

The liquidation period should still be six months according to the company law. Bank shareholders should not bear unlimited liability for the savings department.

Recently, in view of the decline in the market in this city and the closure of many silver and money businesses, the Ministry of Finance is deeply concerned that the progress will be hindered, and has promulgated six supervision and liquidation methods, and selected supervisors to supervise the progress. The National Association of Accountants believes that it is timely and important, but has some opinions on the second and fourth items, and has presented them to the Ministry of Finance. The original text is recorded below:

To: The petition is for the supervision and liquidation methods to be corrected according to law. On June 6, the newspaper reported that the Ministry of Finance issued instructions to the silver and money industries associations, stipulating six supervision and liquidation methods, and commissioned commissioners to supervise the liquidation of the recently closed firms and banks, so that the law can effectively protect the people, correct accumulated bad habits, and benefit merchants and people. The members of the association and the members of the affiliated associations are mostly accountants who perform their duties. They deeply feel that in the years since they have been carrying out liquidation cases, merchants and people have been used to accumulated bad habits and have not followed laws, and persuasion is ineffective, and difficulties arise during the process. Some members have also reported the difficulties to judicial and administrative officials, asking for supervision, but every time they are restricted by the fact that there is no precedent to refer to. Now that the Ministry of Finance has issued a new order for supervision and liquidation, they are deeply admired. However, the second item, which stipulates that the liquidation period is limited to three months, seems to be different from the provision in Article 61 of the Company Law that the liquidator should complete the liquidation within six months. According to the liquidation matters, the case involves hundreds of thousands of people. The Ministry of Finance sympathizes with the people's difficulties, so it is appropriate to order them to proceed as soon as possible, but the liquidation cases, procedures, and procedures are very detailed and prudent by law, and it takes a lot of time to proceed in order. For example, the Provisional Regulations for the Liquidation of Merchants' Debts stipulate that the period for reporting claims is 14 days to one month, and if there are branches and agents in remote places, the period may be extended. It also stipulates that the date of the creditors' meeting must be seven days to one month after the expiration of the claim reporting period. This only refers to the two items of reporting claims and convening a creditors' meeting, which already have a three-month limit. As for other matters, it will also take a considerable amount of time, not to mention the occurrence of various matters that hinder the processing in Article 16 of the Provisional Regulations for the Liquidation of Merchants' Debts. It is inevitable that there will be a delay in time. Instead of setting a limit that is difficult to implement, it is better to follow the provisions of the Company Law, so that it is consistent with the current legal system. In addition, Item 4 of the supervision and liquidation methods stipulates that if the assets are discounted and the debts cannot be fully offset, a bank organized as a joint-stock limited company should apply for bankruptcy according to law. The remaining banks or money houses organized as joint-stock limited companies that also operate savings business should impose joint and several unlimited liability on the managers, directors, supervisors, and shareholders according to law. According to Article 15 of the Savings Bank Law, if the assets of the savings bank are insufficient to repay the debts of the depositors, the directors and supervisors shall bear joint and several unlimited liability, and there is no provision for shareholders to bear joint and several unlimited liability. Although a bank organized as a joint-stock limited company also operates savings business, its shareholders should still be shareholders of a limited company. If the assets are insufficient to offset the debts due to the poor management of the savings department, the directors and supervisors are responsible to the shareholders. Therefore, their joint and several unlimited liability is only limited to the savings department. The shareholders of a bank organized as a joint-stock limited company that does not operate savings business should not be changed from limited to unlimited, nor should the directors and supervisors of a bank organized as a joint-stock limited company that does not operate savings business be liable for all debts of the bank. Therefore, it is proposed that the Ministry of Finance amend it according to law to "The remaining banks or money houses should impose joint and several unlimited liability on the managers, directors, supervisors, and shareholders according to law. Banks organized as joint-stock limited companies that also operate savings business should impose joint and several unlimited liability on the directors and supervisors for the debts of the savings department." The association has not received any clear instructions, but it is only based on newspaper reports, and it is not dare to speculate whether it is consistent with the original text. However, because the merchants and people of our country may not be familiar with the legal system, and if they see the words "joint and several unlimited liability", they are afraid that doubts will arise and the shadow will be great. We humbly offer our humble opinions, hoping that they will be adopted and revised, which will be a great blessing for merchants and people.

Special Issue for the Inaugural Meeting of the Chinese Children's Culture Association

Preparatory Process of the Association Lin Yin

(1) Motivation

When the association was initiated, there were only three of us, He Gongchao, Huang Jiping, and myself. We casually talked during our spare time. We felt that the output and quality of Chinese children's books were problematic. Although there was a large quantity, the quality was very poor. In particular, the content and form of general reading materials were only suitable for children to memorize and not for them to use actively. Therefore, we wanted to organize a group to connect authors of children's books and elementary school teachers to critique the existing children's books and newspapers, and on the one hand, create new books and newspapers. With this goal in mind, we drafted a preamble and a few simple articles of association to solicit opinions from our acquaintances. This was around July or August last year. By February of this year, more than twenty people had signed that opinion paper. Especially Dong Chuncai, Bai... they were very enthusiastic. At this time, Gongchao and I jointly issued a notice to hold the first initiators' meeting.

(2) Initiators' Meeting

Nineteen comrades attended this initiators' meeting. Everyone was very excited and expressed their opinions on the organization of the association. They believed that children's cultural work was not limited to books and newspapers. While the current issues with books and newspapers needed criticism and creation, other aspects of children's cultural work required our efforts even more. Moreover, this work could not be borne by a few of us alone. It was necessary to unite elementary school teachers, children's newspaper editors, illustrators, the publishing industry, and parents of children across the country to jointly shoulder the responsibility. Therefore, it was decided that the association would be named the Chinese Children's Culture Association, with the purpose of studying children's issues and promoting children's culture. More comrades would be sought to join as initiators to expand our scope of work and work together. Subsequently, Huang Jingwan, Hu Shuyi, Chen Jicheng, Xu Fengchang, Wei Bingxin, Ma Chonggan, and Sun Yucai all enthusiastically joined. We held the first initiators' meeting on March 24th. More than forty people attended. On the one hand, we proceeded with the organizational formalities, and on the other hand, we began to do a lot of practical work.

(3) Work During the Preparatory Period

Of course, this short three-month preparatory period was very rushed. Moreover, Children's Day was also within our preparatory period. At that time, although we had not yet received the approval document from the Municipal Party Department to organize, the work was already in front of us, and we had to do it. Therefore, we sent representatives to participate in celebrations in several places where gatherings were held, and distributed the association's views on current children's cultural work. We also invited Comrade Wei Bingxin to broadcast a speech on the radio at the Sino-Western Radio Station about Children's Day and family education. Soon, the approval document from the Municipal Party Department came down. We immediately organized a preparatory committee to speed up the establishment. We also edited a series of books titled "Children of Today," inviting educators and scholars with specialized research from across the country to contribute articles, with the intention of publishing them at the opening of Children's Year to serve as a reference for comrades serving in the children's ranks of Children's Year. To expand the association's foundation and strengthen its power, the initiators' meeting resolved that each initiator must solicit at least five members. In order to make the association's work practical, it was necessary to bridge the gap between adults and children. Therefore, it was decided to welcome children to join the association, with a membership fee of only two jiao per year, so that children would not have an excessive burden. At this time, Shanghai was also launching a campaign to eradicate illiteracy. We immediately felt that this was an opportunity for practical work. In this campaign, children should be the focus of practical experiments. We first specially invited the Huacun Public Basic School and the Yingye Elementary School to implement literacy service groups using the "little teacher" system, and appointed Huang Jingwan and Sun Yucai as instructors to guide the little teachers on how to participate in this important work in the community. Starting this month, we also regularly broadcast children's education issues and children's programs every week on the Xin Xin Radio Station. Although we only had a short three-month preparatory period, the current work has already forced us to not delay the establishment any longer. The enthusiasm for organizing branches everywhere and the many tasks that must be started after the establishment are all reasons why we decided to hold the inaugural meeting today. Of course, during the initial stage, many tasks cannot satisfy everyone's wishes. We only hope that after the establishment, all members can work faithfully. This is not only the glory of the association, but also the happiness of children across the country. My simple and intermittent report, of course, cannot avoid omissions. I hope the comrades will forgive me.

The World of Children Wei Bingxin 112

"The 20th century is the century of children," this sentence has been recognized worldwide. Indeed, to build a progressive society and create a world of great harmony, we can only hope for the next generation of children. The future world is the world of children, and modern children are the backbone of building society and creating the world in the future.

Look, the modern warlords and militarists around the world, who are addicted to war and vying for territory, only have the ambition to dominate and seize power. Where do they have the grand vision of creating a peaceful world?

Look, the modern politicians around the world, who abuse their authority and stir up trouble, only have the idea of becoming high officials and seeking profit. Where do they have plans to build a good society?

Look, the modern farmers and laborers around the world, who shed blood and sweat and sell their labor, can only seek food and clothing for themselves and avoid freezing and starvation. They lack the power to weave and shoulder the responsibility of building society and transforming the world.

Look, the modern scholars around the world, who study knowledge and sell it, can only sell their articles and seek a livelihood for themselves. They rarely shoulder the responsibility of building society and transforming the world.

However, although the lofty ideals of modern humanity have been hindered by human power and various environmental obstacles and cannot be realized, if we do not advocate, promote, and strive hard, in the next generation, we will surely be able to create a paradise for humanity, bloom bright flowers, and bear sweet fruits. All problems, whether personal, family, social, national, or worldwide, can be resolved satisfactorily.

Especially in our country, which was once a colony in the international arena, to break away from the oppression of imperialism and obtain true independence and equality, it is necessary for the children to continue to work hard in the future in order to have the possibility of realization.

Therefore, the modern children's issue is really the key to all issues. It is the fundamental issue of all issues. In modern China, we must especially focus on the children's issue with all our strength and cultivate new Chinese children who can shoulder the responsibility of building a progressive society and creating a world of great harmony in the future.

The Chinese Children's Culture Association is shouldering this mission. However, this mission is indeed too great. I hope that people across the country who are engaged in children's cultural work will join our group and work together.

How Is Our Work? He Gongchao 113

The purpose of this association is to engage in various cultural activities within the scope of children (including literature, art, sports...). But don't think that as long as it is cultural work, it is beneficial to children. If we still tell children stories that end with becoming officials and getting rich, and teach children to sing songs like "Taohua Jiang," are we benefiting children or harming them? The work of this association should obviously be the opposite of these, or to put it more precisely, it should be:

Collective and aesthetic, not individualistic. We want to enable children to engage in activities as a group, so that they understand that within a group, everyone has the right to equal development and enjoyment, and oppose those activities that cultivate children's individualistic heroic thoughts and desires for leadership.

Striving, not enjoying. Even if we organize a children's trip, we will definitely not prepare a special train and invite the children to relax in those scenic spots. Instead, we should have the children take the train and visit on their own, like the children of a certain elementary school in Huai'an, so that they can experience the cold looks of the station staff and know the dangers on the road of life, and let them visit the Indian "Asan" and compatriots in the slums of Shanghai and know the pain of being slaves and becoming slaves.

For the majority, not for the minority. Our work should focus on the poor children who make up more than 90% of the country. Therefore, geographically speaking, we should not only circle in the residential areas of Shanghai, but should develop towards the countryside and factory areas. In terms of knowledge level, we should not only deal with school children, but should shake hands with illiterate children. In terms of wealth standards, we should not only know how to please the children of wealthy families, but should strive for those poor children who have no clothes or food.

Forward-looking, not backward-looking. The thoughts and concepts contained in all our work (such as a children's song, a story, a music broadcast) should be progressive, revolutionary, active, and optimistic, and should not be passive, pessimistic, or unrevolutionary. We also oppose superstitious legends, bizarre stories, the concept of cause and effect, and the idea of retreating from life, such as hermitage in the mountains and forests.

If the work of this association follows the path described above, it will be able to fulfill its necessary mission in this historical stage. Otherwise, it may fall into becoming an agency that merely decorates the era of peace.

The Twentieth Century Is the Century of Children Chen Jicheng Sun Yucai 114

The 20th century is a century in which the women's rights movement has led to the expansion of children's rights. Ellen Key simply called this "the century of children." The importance of children-centeredness has long been felt in various countries around the world, and deep attention has been paid to children's affairs, which are also developing. Soviet Russia is a socialist country. They not only widely establish nurseries to educate the children of ordinary workers, but also have many special organizations, such as children's science research institutes and children's art research institutes, to fully cultivate children's physical and mental development. Italy is a fascist country. Their training for young party members is divided into three stages. While exercising their physique, they also teach party ideology. They also believe that educating children is one of the most important undertakings of the country. After the war, Germany always had the determination to seek revenge and revive the country. While developing science and striving for construction, it also paid attention to children's education in order to cultivate the foundation of the country. Children are the future masters of the country. China's most basic and important work in seeking national rejuvenation and family prosperity is to pay attention to children's affairs. The Chinese Children's Culture Association is a new group that pays attention to children's cultural affairs. Here, we are all willing to seek welfare for children. To put it bluntly, it is also to work hard for the national rejuvenation movement.

Education News 147

Key Points of the Implementation Outline of People's Education 148

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 15th) The Ministry of Education announced the implementation rules of the Implementation Outline of People's Education on the 15th. The key points are as follows: (1) Short-term elementary schools are exempt from tuition and book fees, (2) School-age children who are healthy and live in the local area where elementary schools are established should be supervised to attend school. Those who do not comply will be fined on their parents, (3) All regions should divide elementary school districts, investigate school-age children, plan locations, and raise funds, (4) The first phase of compulsory education implementation measures will be from the 24th to the 28th year as the period for popularizing one year of compulsory education, (5) The first phase of implementation measures will be from the 29th to the 33rd year as the period for popularizing two years of compulsory education, (6) The third phase of implementation measures will be from the 24th year onwards, in addition to the various measures of the first phase, will continue to be implemented, two-year elementary schools in various places should be gradually changed to four-year ordinary elementary schools, (7) Administrative organs at all levels, the central government is organized by the Ministry of Education, the provinces and cities are organized by the competent educational administrative organs, (8) Teacher training, each province and city implements compulsory education, promotes the establishment of short-term elementary schools, there must be many teachers, should establish short-term elementary school teacher training classes in provincial, municipal, or county junior high schools and normal schools,

The Ministry of Education Announces the Detailed Rules for the Master's Degree Examination 149

The Ministry of Education announced twelve detailed rules for the master's degree examination on the 14th. The original text is as follows:

Article 1 These detailed rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 4, Paragraph 3 of the Degree Granting Law.

Article 2 Candidates for the master's degree shall have the following qualifications in accordance with the provisions of Article 4, Paragraph 1, Articles 9 and 10 of the Degree Granting Law, and Articles 7 and 9 of the Provisional Organization Regulations of University Graduate Schools and Research Institutes: (1) Have received a bachelor's degree in accordance with the Degree Granting Law, or have graduated from a university or independent college in the country, public or private, before the implementation of the Degree Granting Law, or have obtained a degree equivalent to a bachelor's degree from a foreign university recognized by the Ministry of Education, (2) Have continued to study in a graduate school or research institute as stipulated in Article 4 of the Degree Granting Law for more than two years, (3) Have completed the prescribed courses, completed the research thesis, and have been certified as passing the grade by the department or institute to which they belong in the form of regular examinations and audits.

Article 3 The master's degree examination is divided into the following two types: (1) Subject examination, (2) Thesis examination. The subject examination shall be conducted in writing for two or more subjects related to the thesis designated by the examination committee from the subjects taken by the candidate. If necessary, an experimental examination may also be held in the laboratory. The thesis examination shall be conducted in the form of an oral examination in which the examination committee raises questions on the thesis submitted by the candidate. If necessary, a written examination may also be held. The subject examination and the thesis examination shall be held at the end of the second semester of each academic year. The date and time shall be determined by the Master's Degree Examination Committee.

Article 4 Candidates must submit two copies each of the revised research thesis and thesis abstract to the department or institute to which they belong one month before the examination period, and the department or institute shall submit them to the examination committee. The thesis and abstract must be written in the national language, but a copy written in a foreign language may be submitted at the same time. The thesis that has been obtained for other degrees may not be submitted again.

Article 5 The calculation of examination results shall be as follows: the thesis grade shall account for 60%, and the subject grade shall account for 40%. Both grades must be 60 points or above to be considered passing. Those who fail the examination must continue to study in the department or institute to which they belong for one year before they can resubmit the thesis and take the entire examination.

Article 6 Candidates who have studied for two years and wish to continue studying in the department or institute may request a one-year extension and submit the thesis for examination in the next session.

Article 7 The Master's Degree Examination Committee shall be organized in accordance with the provisions of Article 8, Paragraph 2 of the Provisional Organization Regulations of University Graduate Schools, by the school hiring a number of internal and external members approved by the Ministry of Education (each accounting for half). One person shall be designated by the Ministry as the chairman of the committee. When necessary, this member may also be designated by the Ministry. The director of the research institute and a professor in charge of guiding the candidate's research work shall be ex officio members.

Article 8 The review of each candidate's thesis shall be conducted by two external members. At least one external member must participate in and preside over the oral or written examination. At least one external member must participate in and preside over the subject examination.

Article 9 After the examination results of the candidates have been separately evaluated by the chief examiners, they must be submitted to the committee for final decision by all members.

Article 10 The theses (with a copy of the abstract), examination papers, and various grades of candidates who have passed the examination shall be reviewed by the school and submitted to the Ministry within one month after the completion of the examination.

Article 11 Graduate students enrolled by research institutes established with the approval of the Ministry in accordance with the Provisional Organization Regulations of University Graduate Schools in the 23rd year of the Republic of China and subsequent years shall be granted a master's degree by the university or independent college if they pass the examination in accordance with these detailed rules upon the expiration of their study period and are reviewed by the Ministry without objection.

Article 12 These detailed rules shall be formulated and promulgated by the Ministry of Education for implementation.
